## Chapter 19: Computational Design XII: Presentations:

### Section: 19.2 Presentations in Rule Application and Parametric Design:

Presentations play a crucial role in computational design, allowing designers to effectively communicate their ideas and designs to others. In this section, we will explore the role of presentations in rule application and parametric design and how they can enhance the design process.

#### 19.2a Presentations in Non-deterministic Rule Application

In computational design, rules are used to define relationships and constraints between different elements of a design. These rules can be deterministic, meaning they always produce the same result, or non-deterministic, meaning they can produce different results based on certain conditions. Non-deterministic rules are particularly useful in parametric design, where a design is defined by a set of parameters that can be varied to produce different outcomes.

Presentations in non-deterministic rule application are essential for understanding and communicating the potential variations in a design. By visualizing the different outcomes of a non-deterministic rule, designers can better understand the impact of different parameters on the final design. This can also aid in the decision-making process, as designers can compare and contrast the different variations to determine which one best fits their design goals.

One way to present non-deterministic rule application is through the use of diagrams and graphs. These visual representations can show the relationship between different parameters and the resulting variations in the design. For example, a scatter plot can be used to show how changing a specific parameter affects the overall shape of a design. This type of presentation can help designers identify patterns and trends in the data, allowing them to make more informed decisions about their design.

Another way to present non-deterministic rule application is through the use of interactive simulations. These simulations allow designers to manipulate the parameters in real-time and see the resulting variations in the design. This type of presentation can be particularly useful for complex designs with multiple parameters, as it allows for a more intuitive understanding of the design space.

In conclusion, presentations in non-deterministic rule application are crucial for understanding and communicating the potential variations in a design. By using visual representations and interactive simulations, designers can better explore and communicate the possibilities of their designs, leading to more informed and innovative solutions.

In non-deterministic shape generation, presentations are crucial for showcasing the potential of a design. This can be particularly useful in fields such as architecture and product design, where the end-user may have specific preferences or requirements.

Whether through diagrams, graphs, or interactive simulations, presentations enhance the design process and aid in decision-making, ultimately leading to more innovative and effective designs. 


## Chapter 19: Computational Design XII: Presentations:

### Section: 19.2 Presentations in Rule Application and Parametric Design:

Presentations play a crucial role in computational design, allowing designers to effectively communicate their ideas and designs to others. In this section, we will explore the role of presentations in rule application and parametric design and how they can enhance the design process.

#### 19.2a Presentations in Non-deterministic Rule Application

In computational design, rules are used to define relationships and constraints between different elements of a design. These rules can be deterministic, meaning they always produce the same result, or non-deterministic, meaning they can produce different results based on certain conditions. Non-deterministic rules are particularly useful in parametric design, where a design is defined by a set of parameters that can be varied to produce different outcomes.

Presentations in non-deterministic rule application are essential for understanding and communicating the potential variations in a design. By visualizing the different outcomes of a non-deterministic rule, designers can better understand the impact of different parameters on the final design. This can also aid in the decision-making process, as designers can compare and contrast the different variations to determine which one best fits their design goals.

One way to present non-deterministic rule application is through the use of diagrams and graphs. These visual representations can show the relationship between different parameters and the resulting variations in the design. For example, a scatter plot can be used to show how changing a specific parameter affects the overall shape of a design. This type of presentation can help designers identify patterns and trends in the data, allowing them to make more informed decisions about their design.

Another way to present non-deterministic rule application is through the use of interactive simulations. These simulations allow designers to manipulate the parameters in real-time and see the resulting variations in the design. This can be particularly useful for complex designs with multiple parameters, as it allows for a more intuitive understanding of the design space.

#### 19.2b Presentations in Deterministic Rule Application

While non-deterministic rules allow for a range of variations in a design, deterministic rules produce a single, consistent result. However, presentations are still important in deterministic rule application as they can help designers understand the underlying logic and reasoning behind the design.

One way to present deterministic rule application is through the use of flowcharts or decision trees. These visual representations can show the sequence of rules and conditions that lead to the final design. This can help designers understand the logic behind the design and make any necessary adjustments or improvements.

Another way to present deterministic rule application is through the use of animations. By visualizing the step-by-step application of rules, designers can gain a better understanding of how the design evolves and how each rule contributes to the final result.

#### 19.2c Presentations in Parametric Design

Parametric design is a powerful tool in computational design, allowing for the creation of complex and highly customizable designs. Presentations play a crucial role in parametric design, as they allow designers to communicate the design intent and showcase the potential variations in the design.

One way to present parametric design is through the use of generative design tools. These tools use algorithms and rules to generate a range of design options based on a set of parameters. By presenting these options, designers can showcase the potential of their design and gather feedback from stakeholders.

Another way to present parametric design is through the use of physical models or prototypes. These physical representations allow for a more tangible understanding of the design and its variations. They can also be used to test the functionality and feasibility of the design.

In conclusion, presentations are an essential aspect of computational design, allowing designers to effectively communicate their ideas and designs. Whether in non-deterministic or deterministic rule application, or in parametric design, presentations play a crucial role in enhancing the design process and aiding in decision-making.
